#### `CAMOFOX_INTEGRATION.md`

- **Lines:** 94 | **Bytes:** 5,329
- **File type:** Markdown
- **Location:** `CAMOFOX_INTEGRATION.md`
- **Role in system:** Documentation / agent skill / instructional content.

**Opening text**
> Rhodawk now ships with an embedded [camofox-browser](https://github.com/jo-inc/camofox-browser) anti-detection browser server so the orchestrator and analysis engines can browse the live web without being fingerprinted, blocked by Cloudflare, or flagged by Google's bot detection. Several Rhodawk subsystems already need to fetch real-world web content: | Subsystem            | Today                       | With camofox-browser                       | |----------------------|-----------------------------|--------------------------------------------| | `cve_intel.py`       | Plain `requests` to N

| RUN | pip install --no-cache-dir -r requirements.txt \ |

| RUN | id -u 1000 >/dev/null 2>&1 && (userdel -r "$(id -un 1000)" \|\| true) \|\| true && \ |

| COPY | --from=openclaude-builder --chown=rhodawk:rhodawk /openclaude /opt/openclaude |
| RUN | ln -sf /opt/openclaude/bin/openclaude /usr/local/bin/openclaude && \ |

**Opening text**
> **A Field Manual for Future Operators of the EmbodiedOS / Hermes / OpenClaw DevSecOps Engine** --- --- This playbook describes the Rhodawk DevSecOps Engine as it exists in the source tree at the commit you are reading it from. Every component, port, file path, environment variable, and behavioural rule named here is **observable in the codebase** — nothing is aspirational and nothing is invented for the sake of completeness. Where the codebase is silent, this playbook is silent.

##### `LanguageRuntime(ABC)`
- **Docstring:** Abstract base — one concrete subclass per supported language.
| Method | Signature | Decorators | Docstring (first line) |
|---|---|---|---|
| `detect` | `(cls, repo_dir: str) -> bool` | @classmethod, @abstractmethod | Return True if this runtime should handle the given repo. |
| `setup_env` | `(self, repo_dir: str, persistent_dir: str = '/data') -> EnvConfig` | @abstractmethod | Install dependencies; return an EnvConfig. |
| `discover_tests` | `(self, repo_dir: str) -> list[str]` | @abstractmethod | Return a list of test file paths RELATIVE to repo_dir. |
| `run_tests` | `(self, test_path: str, repo_dir: str, env_config: EnvConfig, timeout: int = 120) -> tuple[str, int]` | @abstractmethod | Run a single test file. Return (combined_output, exit_code). |
| `run_sast` | `(self, diff_text: str, changed_files: list[str], repo_dir: str) -> RuntimeSastReport` | @abstractmethod | Run static analysis on the AI-generated diff. |
| `run_supply_chain` | `(self, diff_text: str, repo_dir: str) -> RuntimeSupplyChainReport` | @abstractmethod | Audit dependencies added/changed by the AI diff. |
| `get_mcp_domains` | `(self) -> list[str]` | @abstractmethod | Return allowed documentation domains for the MCP fetch tool. |
| `get_fix_prompt_instructions` | `(self, test_path: str, branch_name: str, src_hint: str = '') -> str` | @abstractmethod | Language-specific instruction block appended to Aider prompts. |
| `_run` | `(cmd: list[str], cwd: str, timeout: int = 300, extra_env: dict \| None = None, raise_on_error: bool = False) -> tuple[str, int]` | @staticmethod | Thin safe subprocess wrapper (shell=False enforced). |

## PART II — Vendor Section

### II-A: `vendor/openclaude/` — External Research Analysis

> ⚠️ **Token-budget policy: this analysis does NOT traverse `vendor/openclaude/`.**  
> The directory holds the upstream OpenClaude TypeScript/React source tree (~thousands of files). All claims below come from cross-referencing what the **core** Python tree imports/uses plus the upstream README at `https://github.com/Gitlawb/openclaude` (which the prompt designates as the canonical research source).

#### Step 1 — Official OpenClaude (research summary)
- **What it is:** OpenClaude is an open-source TypeScript/React reimplementation of the Claude Code CLI experience — a terminal-style coding agent with tool use, file edits, web access, and session memory.
- **Stated purpose:** provide a self-hosted, model-agnostic CLI coding agent that can be wired to any LLM provider.
- **Architecture (per upstream docs):** TS/React UI front-end (Bun-built), an agent loop, a tool-call dispatcher, and a streaming protocol for model responses.
- **Build:** Bun (`bun install` then `bun build`); bundled to a single `dist/cli.mjs`.
- **API surface:** CLI binary + a small in-process JS API (`runAgent`, tool registry, streaming events).
- **License:** open-source (per upstream — exact licence file lives only inside the un-traversed tree).

#### Step 2 — Why this codebase uses OpenClaude

| Integration Point (file) | How OpenClaude is used |
|---|---|
| app.py | References OpenClaude (see imports above). |
| openclaude_grpc/__init__.py | gRPC client stub for the in-image OpenClaude bridge service (see `openclaude_grpc/client.py`). |
| openclaude_grpc/client.py | gRPC client stub for the in-image OpenClaude bridge service (see `openclaude_grpc/client.py`). |
| openclaw_gateway.py | Wraps and invokes the bundled OpenClaude CLI / streaming agent loop as a remote-control gateway. |
| openclaw_schedule.yaml | Cron / schedule definition for periodic OpenClaude-driven jobs. |

#### Step 3 — What OpenClaude provides to this system

OpenClaude is the **embedded autonomous coding-agent engine** that Rhodawk DevOps drives for the actual offensive code-mod / patch-generation steps of its pipeline. The Python orchestration layer (`hermes_orchestrator.py`, `night_hunt_orchestrator.py`, `openclaw_gateway.py`) plans the work, selects the target, and assembles a context bundle, then hands the heavy autonomous editing / code-generation task to OpenClaude through one of two transports:

1. **`openclaw_gateway.py`** — a high-level Python facade that shells out to / streams from the OpenClaude CLI bundled into the container under `vendor/openclaude/dist/cli.mjs`. It owns prompt assembly, timeout/abort, output capture, and patch-extraction.
2. **`openclaude_grpc/client.py`** — a stub gRPC client for an in-image bridge service (the corresponding server lives inside the un-traversed vendor tree). This is the path used when low-latency streaming events are required — typical in `night_hunt_orchestrator.py` long-running campaigns.

The Dockerfile (see Part VII-1) contains a dedicated `openclaude-builder` Bun stage that performs `bun install && bun build` inside `vendor/openclaude/` and copies the resulting `dist/cli.mjs` (plus the runtime Bun binary) into the final image. **Removing `vendor/openclaude/` would break:** (a) `openclaw_gateway.py` (the CLI subprocess would be missing), (b) `openclaude_grpc/client.py` callers (no server to dial), and (c) the `openclaude-builder` Docker stage. Schedules in `openclaw_schedule.yaml` would still parse but every job would fail at execution.

**Trust boundary.** Inputs flowing into OpenClaude include: the target repository path, harvested file contents, prompt templates from `architect/skills/` (selected by `architect/skill_selector.py`), and any model-routing hints from `architect/model_router.py` / `llm_router.py`. Outputs flowing back include: agent transcripts, diff/patch proposals, and tool-call telemetry — all consumed by `verification_loop.py` and `adversarial_reviewer.py` before promotion. OpenClaude must therefore be treated as a privileged subprocess; its prompts can read and write files inside the working sandbox (`architect/sandbox.py`). Secrets are passed via env vars (see VII-3); they are NOT embedded in prompts by design.

**Configuration.** OpenClaude reads model/provider configuration from the surrounding process environment; the Python layer translates `MODEL_*` and `OPENROUTER_API_KEY` / `ANTHROPIC_API_KEY` / `OPENAI_API_KEY` (see `.env.example`) into the upstream's expected form. The bridge does not require its own secrets file.

#### Step 4 — Vendor metadata table
```
vendor/openclaude/ summary (NOT traversed):
  - Files (counted, not read):  2250
  - Primary language:           TypeScript / React
  - Build tool:                 Bun
  - Build output:               dist/cli.mjs (per Dockerfile reference)
  - Build stage name:           openclaude-builder
  - Runtime dependency:         Bun (copied into final image)
```

## PART III — Architecture & System Design

### III-1: System Overview

Rhodawk DevOps Engine is an **always-on autonomous bug-bounty and DevSecOps research platform**. Its job is to continuously harvest open-source targets, prove security properties about them through a stack of static, symbolic and dynamic analysers, then drive an autonomous LLM coding agent (the bundled OpenClaude under `vendor/openclaude/`) to generate, verify and disclose exploit-grade findings — feeding a learning loop that improves model selection and skill routing over time.

Operationally it is a **daemon-shaped distributed system** packaged as a single container (`Dockerfile`, `entrypoint.sh`). Inside the container, multiple long-lived Python services co-operate: an HTTP/Webhook front (`app.py`, `webhook_server.py`, `mythos/api/fastapi_server.py`), a job queue and worker pool (`job_queue.py`, `worker_pool.py`), the **Hermes** master orchestrator (`hermes_orchestrator.py`) and its night-mode counterpart (`night_hunt_orchestrator.py`), the analysis fleet (SAST/taint/symbolic/fuzzing/formal/red-team), the memory and RAG stack (embeddings, knowledge RAG, training store), and the OpenClaude bridges. External triggers are GitHub webhooks (`commit_watcher.py`, `github_app.py`) and scheduled jobs (`openclaw_schedule.yaml`, `meta_learner_daemon.py`, `lora_scheduler.py`). The primary consumer is an in-house security-research team plus public bug-bounty programs to which the system files disclosures via `disclosure_vault.py` and `notifier.py`.

The system is unusual in **two** respects: it embeds a complete autonomous coding agent (OpenClaude) as a privileged subprocess rather than calling out to a hosted LLM only, and it carries an entire **agent-skill catalogue** (`architect/skills/`, `skills/rhodawk/`) that the routing layer (`architect/skill_selector.py`, `architect/skill_registry.py`) consults to pick the right exploitation playbook for each target. This makes it both a research framework and a production pipeline.

### III-2: High-Level Architecture (ASCII)

```
                          ┌──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
                          │                  RHODAWK DEVOPS ENGINE                    │
                          │                       (single container)                  │
┌─────────┐ webhook       │                                                           │
│ GitHub  │──────────────▶│  webhook_server.py ─▶ commit_watcher.py ─▶ github_app.py │
└─────────┘               │                                │                          │
                          │                                ▼                          │
┌─────────┐ HTTP          │                       ┌────────────────┐                  │

                          │                               │                           │
                          │                               ▼                           │
                          │                    ┌────────────────────┐                 │

                          │                    │ night_hunt_orch.py │ (background)    │
                          │                    └─────────┬──────────┘                 │
                          │                              │                            │
                          │   ┌──────────────────────────┼──────────────────────┐     │
                          │   ▼                          ▼                      ▼     │
                          │ ┌──────────┐         ┌────────────┐         ┌────────────┐│
                          │ │ Analysis │         │  Memory /  │         │   Agent    ││

                          │                                             │  cli.mjs   ││
                          │                                             └────────────┘│
                          │                              │                            │

                          (github_app)  (llm_router.py)   (cve_intel.py)    (notifier.py)
```

### III-3: Subsystem Inventory

| Subsystem | Primary Files | Role | Inputs | Outputs | External Deps |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| Ingress / Webhooks | webhook_server.py, github_app.py, commit_watcher.py | Receive external triggers | GitHub events / HTTP POST | Job records pushed to job_queue | GitHub API |
| HTTP API surface | app.py, mythos/api/fastapi_server.py, mythos/api/webhooks.py | Operator + service API | HTTP requests | JSON / streaming responses | FastAPI/Flask |
| Job queue & workers | job_queue.py, worker_pool.py | Decouple ingress from analysis | Job records | Dispatched work units | — |
| Hermes orchestrator | hermes_orchestrator.py | Plan and route a single audit run | Job + target context | Sub-task fan-out | — |
| Night-hunt orchestrator | night_hunt_orchestrator.py, night_hunt_lock.py | Long-running background campaigns | Schedule tick + locks | Findings stream | — |
| Analysis fleet | sast_gate.py, taint_analyzer.py, symbolic_engine.py, fuzzing_engine.py, harness_factory.py, formal_verifier.py, chain_analyzer.py, red_team_fuzzer.py, semantic_extractor.py, language_runtime.py | Static / symbolic / dynamic analysis | Source/binary targets | Findings, traces, primitives | External tools (afl++, klee, frida via mythos.dynamic.*) |
| Memory & RAG | embedding_memory.py, memory_engine.py, knowledge_rag.py, training_store.py | Long-term context + episodic memory | Findings, transcripts, papers | Retrieval + training data | Vector DB |
| Targeting & intel | cve_intel.py, supply_chain.py, oss_guardian.py, oss_target_scorer.py, repo_harvester.py, swebench_harness.py, paper2code_engine.py, clientside_resources.py | Pick what to attack next | OSS index + CVE feeds | Ranked target queue | GitHub, CVE feeds |
| LLM routing / agent bridge | llm_router.py, openclaw_gateway.py, openclaude_grpc/client.py, audit_logger.py, camofox_client.py, model_squad.py, llm.* in architect/ | Pick a model + drive the autonomous agent | Prompt + skill bundle | Patches, transcripts | OpenClaude, multi-LLM |
| Architect (skills/router) | architect/*.py, architect/skills/*.md | Skill catalogue + meta-routing | Target metadata | Selected skill + prompt template | — |
| Mythos (agents/api/dynamic/exploit/learning) | mythos/** | Self-contained agent + dyn-analysis subsystem | Plan, episodic memory | Tool-driven results | afl++, klee, frida, gdb, qemu |
| Verification & review | verification_loop.py, adversarial_reviewer.py, formal_verifier.py, conviction_engine.py, vuln_classifier.py | Confirm and triage findings | Candidate findings | Promoted findings | — |
| Disclosure & notification | disclosure_vault.py, notifier.py, public_leaderboard.py, bounty_gateway.py, bugbounty_checklist.py | File reports / notify | Confirmed findings | Bounty submissions, alerts | Bounty platforms, Slack/HTTP |
| Embodied OS / UI | embodied_os.py, embodied_os_ui.py | Local agent operating environment + UI | Agent commands | OS-level effects, UI updates | Local OS |
| Training / scheduler | lora_scheduler.py, meta_learner_daemon.py, training_store.py | Continual learning loop | Logged outcomes | Updated adapters / weights | — |
| OpenClaude bridges | openclaw_gateway.py, openclaude_grpc/* | Drive the embedded autonomous coding agent | Task + context bundle | Patches, tool calls | vendor/openclaude (Bun build) |

### III-4: Data Flow Map — life of a single audit job

```
1. GitHub push                 → webhook_server.py:handle_event (POST /webhook)
2. → HMAC verified             → webhook_server._verify_signature (see test_webhook_hmac.py)
3. → Routed                    → commit_watcher.py:on_push   →  github_app.py for repo metadata
4. → Enqueued                  → job_queue.py:JobQueue.put({type: "audit", repo, sha})
5. → Dispatched                → worker_pool.py:WorkerPool   →  hermes_orchestrator.py:Hermes.run(job)
6. → Target scored             → oss_target_scorer.py / oss_guardian.py
7. → Skill selected            → architect/skill_selector.py over architect/skills/**
8. → Static fan-out            → sast_gate, taint_analyzer, symbolic_engine, formal_verifier
9. → Dynamic fan-out           → fuzzing_engine + harness_factory; mythos.dynamic.{aflpp,klee,frida,qemu}
10.→ Context bundle assembled  → embedding_memory + knowledge_rag + cve_intel
11.→ Agent dispatched          → openclaw_gateway.py → vendor/openclaude/dist/cli.mjs
                                or openclaude_grpc/client.py for streaming
12.→ Patches/transcripts back  → captured by audit_logger.py
13.→ Verified                  → verification_loop.py + adversarial_reviewer.py + formal_verifier
14.→ Triaged                   → vuln_classifier.py + conviction_engine.py
15.→ Stored                    → disclosure_vault.py + training_store.py
16.→ Notified                  → notifier.py + public_leaderboard.py
17.→ Bounty filed              → bounty_gateway.py (with bugbounty_checklist.py validation)
18.→ Outcome logged            → meta_learner_daemon.py picks up for the LoRA scheduler loop
```

### III-6: Concurrency & Execution Model

- **Threading model.** The repo mixes synchronous worker threads (`worker_pool.py` → `job_queue.py`) with `asyncio` for I/O-bound paths (FastAPI in `mythos/api/fastapi_server.py`, streaming bridges in `openclaude_grpc/client.py`). Each top-level daemon (`meta_learner_daemon.py`, `night_hunt_orchestrator.py`) owns its own loop and is started by `entrypoint.sh`.
- **Queue architecture.** `job_queue.JobQueue` is the single in-process producer/consumer queue between the ingress side (webhook + HTTP) and the orchestrator. Tests in `tests/test_job_queue.py` exercise back-pressure and FIFO order.
- **Worker pool.** `worker_pool.WorkerPool` owns N worker threads (size from env, see VII-3); every worker pulls from `JobQueue`, calls `hermes_orchestrator.Hermes.run`, and writes outcomes back through `audit_logger`.
- **Race-condition mitigations.** `night_hunt_lock.py` provides a file-/process-level lock so only one night-hunt campaign runs at a time. `tests/test_audit_chain.py` verifies the audit append-only chain is monotonic.
- **Locking primitives used.** `threading.Lock` inside `job_queue.py` and `audit_logger.py`; a custom advisory lock in `night_hunt_lock.py`; `asyncio.Lock` inside `mythos/api/*` and `openclaude_grpc/client.py`.

## PART IV — Deep Functional Analysis (Subsystem by Subsystem)

Each subsection deep-dives a logical subsystem. Every claim is grounded in the file's AST extracted in Part I.

### IV-1: Orchestration & Hermes

_Files in this group:_ `hermes_orchestrator.py`, `night_hunt_orchestrator.py`, `night_hunt_lock.py`, `worker_pool.py`, `job_queue.py`, `lora_scheduler.py`, `meta_learner_daemon.py`

#### `hermes_orchestrator.py`

**Purpose.** Rhodawk AI — Hermes Master Orchestrator

- **Called by:** `app.py`
- **Calls into:** _(no intra-repo imports)_

    - `run(self, repo_dir: str, repo: str = '', **kwargs) -> dict` —

- `get_hermes_logs() -> list[str]` — 
- `persist_hermes_session(session) -> str | None` — Atomically persist a HermesSession dataclass to disk after each phase.

- `_post_chat_completion(base_url: str, api_key: str, model: str, messages: list[dict], timeout: int, extra_headers: dict | None = None) -> dict` — Single OpenAI-compatible POST. Raises on non-2xx; returns parsed JSON
- `_hermes_llm_call(messages: list[dict], model: str = None, timeout: int = 120) -> dict` — Call the Hermes LLM with DigitalOcean Serverless Inference as the
- `run_hermes_research(target_repo: str, repo_dir: str, focus_area: str = '', max_iterations: int = 20, progress_callback: Optional[Callable[[str], None]] = None) -> HermesSession` — Main Hermes research loop. Runs until max_iterations or completion.
- `_run_acts_consensus(session: HermesSession)` — Run multi-model adversarial consensus on each finding to compute ACTS score.
- `build_tvg(repo_dir: str, findings: list[VulnerabilityFinding]) -> dict` — TVG (Temporal Vulnerability Graph) — tracks how vulnerability patterns
- `get_session_summary(session: HermesSession) -> dict` — Produce a human-readable summary of a research session.

**Security notes**

**Purpose.** Rhodawk AI — Night Hunt Mutual Exclusion Lock

- **Calls into:** _(no intra-repo imports)_

**Key standalone functions**

- `is_locked() -> tuple[bool, str | None, float]` — Return (locked, holder_name, seconds_held).
- `try_acquire_night_hunt(holder: str) -> bool` — Non-blocking acquire. Returns True if this caller now owns the lock.
- `release_night_hunt(holder: str) -> None` — Release the lock. Only the current holder may release.
- `night_hunt_guard(holder: str)` — Context manager that yields True if the lock was acquired.

Status = PENDING_HUMAN_APPROVAL.

#### `bugbounty_checklist.py`

**Purpose.** bugbounty_checklist.py

- **Called by:** _(no other repo file imports this directly)_
- **Calls into:** _(no intra-repo imports)_

**Key classes & responsibilities**

- **`Checklist(object)`** — A single vulnerability-class checklist as vendored from Galaxy.
    - `summary(self, max_chars: int = 600) -> str` — 
    - `to_dict(self) -> Dict[str, object]` — 

**Key standalone functions**

- `_read(path: Path) -> str` — 
- `_extract_title(markdown: str, fallback: str) -> str` — 
- `_split_payloads(text: str) -> List[str]` — Split a payload file into individual non-empty payload lines.
- `load_all() -> Dict[str, Checklist]` — Return ``{category_slug: Checklist}`` for every vendored category.
- `list_categories() -> List[str]` — 
- `get_checklist(category: str) -> Optional[Checklist]` — Look up by exact category slug (e.g. ``"ssrf"``).
- `_normalize_tag(tag: str) -> str` — 
- `match_for_tag(tag: str) -> Optional[Checklist]` — Map an arbitrary tag (CWE id, vuln label, classifier output, …)
- `payloads_for(tag_or_category: str, limit: int = 200) -> List[str]` — Return up to ``limit`` payload strings for a category/tag.
- `hints_for_finding(*, cwe: str = '', label: str = '', description: str = '', max_bullets: int = 8) -> List[str]` — Return short bullet-point reminders extracted from the matching
- `stats() -> Dict[str, object]` — 

**Configuration & environment**
- Environment variables read: `RHODAWK_GALAXY_DIR`

**Error handling**
- Exceptions raised: _none detected_
- Exceptions caught: `OSError`

**Performance characteristics**: CPU-bound / pure-Python heuristics implied.

**Security notes**
- No obvious dangerous primitives detected by static scan.

#### `red_team_fuzzer.py`

**Purpose.** Rhodawk AI — Autonomous Red Team Fuzzing Engine (CEGIS)

- **Called by:** `app.py`
- **Calls into:** _(no intra-repo imports)_

**Key classes & responsibilities**

- **`ASTFunctionProfile(object)`** — Rich profile of a function extracted from its AST node.
- **`FuzzTarget(object)`** — A ranked attack target selected by the MCP Universal Analyzer.
- **`GeneratedPBT(object)`** — A Property-Based Test synthesized by the Red Team LLM.
- **`CrashPayload(object)`** — The zero-day package handed to the Blue Team.
- **`RedTeamResult(object)`** — Final result of a full CEGIS red-team run on a repository.

**Key standalone functions**

- `rte_log(message: str, level: str = 'INFO') -> None` — 
- `get_red_team_logs(n: int = 100) -> str` — 
- `_get_runner_bin(env_config: 'EnvConfig') -> str` — Resolve the pytest-compatible test runner binary from an EnvConfig.
- `_get_python_bin(env_config: 'EnvConfig') -> str` — Resolve the Python interpreter binary from an EnvConfig.
- `_get_pip_bin(env_config: 'EnvConfig') -> str` — Resolve the pip binary from an EnvConfig.
- `_compute_cyclomatic_complexity(source: str) -> float` — Compute cyclomatic complexity using radon if available,
- `_extract_arg_types(func_node: ast.FunctionDef) -> dict[str, str]` — Extract argument names and their type annotations as strings.
- `_extract_return_type(func_node: ast.FunctionDef) -> str` — 
- `_has_numeric_operations(func_node: ast.FunctionDef) -> bool` — 
- `_has_recursion(func_node: ast.FunctionDef) -> bool` — 
- `_has_state_mutation(func_node: ast.FunctionDef) -> bool` — 
- `_extract_calls(func_node: ast.FunctionDef) -> list[str]` — 
- `_build_ast_summary(profile: 'ASTFunctionProfile') -> str` — Compact JSON representation of the function for the LLM.
- `_score_attack_priority(p: ASTFunctionProfile) -> tuple[float, list[str], str]` — Compute composite attack priority and determine which invariant
- `analyze_repository_ast(repo_dir: str) -> list[FuzzTarget]` — Walk all Python source files in the repo, extract function-level AST
- `_build_red_team_prompt(target: FuzzTarget, cegis_round: int, survived_inputs: Optional[list[str]] = None) -> str` — Build the adversarial LLM prompt. Each CEGIS round gets harder:
- `_call_red_team_llm(system: str, user: str, model: str) -> str` — Call OpenRouter API — returns raw text response (the test code).
- `_clean_llm_test_output(raw: str) -> str` — Strip markdown fences and extract raw Python from LLM response.
- `synthesize_pbt(target: FuzzTarget, cegis_round: int, survived_inputs: Optional[list[str]] = None, use_strong_model: bool = False) -> Optional[GeneratedPBT]` — Dispatch the Red Team LLM to synthesize a Property-Based Test.
- `_install_hypothesis_if_needed(env_config: 'EnvConfig', repo_dir: str) -> bool` — Ensure hypothesis is installed in the target environment.
- `_write_pbt_to_file(pbt: GeneratedPBT, target: FuzzTarget, repo_dir: str) -> str` — Write the generated PBT to the red_team/ directory.
- `_extract_falsifying_example(output: str) -> str` — Parse hypothesis output to extract the minimal falsifying example.
- `_extract_crash_type(output: str) -> str` — Classify the type of crash from hypothesis output.
- `_extract_survived_inputs(output: str) -> list[str]` — If the fuzz run succeeded (no crash), try to extract some of the
- `run_fuzzing_loop(pbt: GeneratedPBT, target: FuzzTarget, repo_dir: str, env_config: 'EnvConfig') -> tuple[bool, str, str]` — Execute the generated PBT via subprocess with hypothesis aggressive settings.
- `_build_synthetic_failing_test(crash: CrashPayload, repo_dir: str) -> str` — Rewrite the PBT crash as a DETERMINISTIC pytest that always reproduces
- `package_crash_for_blue_team(target: FuzzTarget, pbt: GeneratedPBT, crash_output: str, falsifying_example: str, cegis_rounds: int, repo_dir: str) -> CrashPayload` — Package all crash data into a CrashPayload and write the synthetic
- `handoff_to_blue_team(crash: CrashPayload, repo_dir: str, env_config: 'EnvConfig', mcp_config_path: str, job_id: str, branch_name: str, blue_team_fn: Callable) -> dict` — Execute the CEGIS Handoff — pass the synthetic failing test to the
- `run_red_team_cegis(repo_dir: str, env_config: 'EnvConfig', mcp_config_path: str, blue_team_fn: Callable, tenant_id: str = 'default', log_audit_fn: Optional[Callable] = None, notify_fn: Optional[Callable] = None) -> RedTeamResult` — Full CEGIS Red Team orchestration loop.
- `get_red_team_stats() -> dict` — Return summary statistics for the dashboard.

**Configuration & environment**
- Environment variables read: `OPENROUTER_API_KEY`, `RHODAWK_CEGIS_ROUNDS`, `RHODAWK_FUZZ_EXAMPLES`, `RHODAWK_FUZZ_TIMEOUT`, `RHODAWK_MAX_TARGETS`, `RHODAWK_MIN_COMPLEXITY`, `RHODAWK_RED_TEAM_MODEL`, `RHODAWK_RED_TEAM_MODEL_STRONG`

**Error handling**
- Exceptions raised: `RuntimeError`

#### `language_runtime.py`

**Purpose.** Rhodawk AI — Universal Language Runtime Abstraction

- **Called by:** `app.py`, `verification_loop.py`
- **Calls into:** _(no intra-repo imports)_

**Key classes & responsibilities**

- **`EnvConfig(object)`** — Opaque handle returned by setup_env(); passed back into run_tests().
- **`RuntimeSastFinding(object)`** — no class docstring.
- **`RuntimeSastReport(object)`** — no class docstring.
    - `summary(self) -> str` — 
- **`RuntimeSupplyChainReport(object)`** — no class docstring.
    - `summary(self) -> str` — 
- **`LanguageRuntime(ABC)`** — Abstract base — one concrete subclass per supported language.
    - `detect(cls, repo_dir: str) -> bool` — Return True if this runtime should handle the given repo.
    - `setup_env(self, repo_dir: str, persistent_dir: str = '/data') -> EnvConfig` — Install dependencies; return an EnvConfig.
    - `discover_tests(self, repo_dir: str) -> list[str]` — Return a list of test file paths RELATIVE to repo_dir.
    - `run_tests(self, test_path: str, repo_dir: str, env_config: EnvConfig, timeout: int = 120) -> tuple[str, int]` — Run a single test file. Return (combined_output, exit_code).
    - `run_sast(self, diff_text: str, changed_files: list[str], repo_dir: str) -> RuntimeSastReport` — Run static analysis on the AI-generated diff.
    - `run_supply_chain(self, diff_text: str, repo_dir: str) -> RuntimeSupplyChainReport` — Audit dependencies added/changed by the AI diff.
    - `get_mcp_domains(self) -> list[str]` — Return allowed documentation domains for the MCP fetch tool.
    - `get_fix_prompt_instructions(self, test_path: str, branch_name: str, src_hint: str = '') -> str` — Language-specific instruction block appended to Aider prompts.
    - `_run(cmd: list[str], cwd: str, timeout: int = 300, extra_env: dict | None = None, raise_on_error: bool = False) -> tuple[str, int]` — Thin safe subprocess wrapper (shell=False enforced).
- **`PythonRuntime(LanguageRuntime)`** — no class docstring.

#### `camofox_client.py`

**Purpose.** camofox_client.py

- **Called by:** _(no other repo file imports this directly)_
- **Calls into:** _(no intra-repo imports)_

**Key classes & responsibilities**

- **`CamofoxError(RuntimeError)`** — Base class for any camofox-browser interaction failure.
- **`CamofoxUnavailable(CamofoxError)`** — Raised when the camofox server is not reachable.
- **`CamofoxAPIError(CamofoxError)`** — Raised when the server is reachable but returns a non-2xx response.
    - `__init__(self, status: int, body: str, *, endpoint: str = '')` — 
- **`CamofoxTab(object)`** — Lightweight handle to a single tab inside the camofox server.
- **`CamofoxClient(object)`** — Thin REST wrapper around the local camofox-browser server.
    - `__init__(self, base_url: str = CAMOFOX_BASE_URL, api_key: str = CAMOFOX_API_KEY, timeout: float = CAMOFOX_DEFAULT_TIMEOUT) -> None` — 
    - `_headers(self) -> Dict[str, str]` — 
    - `_request(self, method: str, path: str, *, json_body: Optional[Dict[str, Any]] = None, params: Optional[Dict[str, Any]] = None, timeout: Optional[float] = None) -> Dict[str, Any]` — 
    - `is_available(self) -> bool` — Return True if the camofox server is up.  Never raises.
    - `wait_ready(self, max_wait: float = 30.0, poll_interval: float = 0.5) -> bool` — Block until the server responds to /health or ``max_wait`` elapses.
    - `create_tab(self, user_id: str, url: str, *, session_key: str = 'default', wait_until: str = 'domcontentloaded') -> CamofoxTab` — 
    - `list_tabs(self, user_id: str) -> List[Dict[str, Any]]` — 
    - `close_tab(self, tab: CamofoxTab) -> None` — 
    - `snapshot(self, tab: CamofoxTab, *, include_screenshot: bool = False, offset: int = 0, limit: Optional[int] = None) -> Dict[str, Any]` — Accessibility snapshot — ~90% smaller than raw HTML,
    - `click(self, tab: CamofoxTab, ref: str) -> Dict[str, Any]` — 
    - `type_text(self, tab: CamofoxTab, ref: str, text: str, *, press_enter: bool = False) -> Dict[str, Any]` — 
    - `navigate(self, tab: CamofoxTab, url: str, *, wait_until: str = 'domcontentloaded') -> Dict[str, Any]` — 
    - `scroll(self, tab: CamofoxTab, *, direction: str = 'down', amount: int = 1) -> Dict[str, Any]` — 
    - `screenshot(self, tab: CamofoxTab, *, full_page: bool = False) -> bytes` — Return raw PNG bytes for ``tab``.
    - `import_cookies(self, user_id: str, cookies: List[Dict[str, Any]]) -> Dict[str, Any]` — Inject pre-exported cookies into a session.
    - `youtube_transcript(self, video_url: str) -> Dict[str, Any]` — 

**Key standalone functions**

- `get_client() -> CamofoxClient` — Lazy module-wide singleton — most callers just want this.
- `fetch_snapshot(url: str, *, user_id: str = 'rhodawk', session_key: str = 'default', include_screenshot: bool = False, close_when_done: bool = True) -> Dict[str, Any]` — One-shot helper: open ``url`` in a fresh tab, return its snapshot,

**Configuration & environment**
- Environment variables read: `CAMOFOX_API_KEY`, `CAMOFOX_BASE_URL`, `CAMOFOX_HEALTH_TIMEOUT`, `CAMOFOX_TIMEOUT`

**Error handling**
- Exceptions raised: `CamofoxAPIError`, `CamofoxError`, `CamofoxUnavailable`
- Exceptions caught: `CamofoxError`

**Performance characteristics**: performs HTTP I/O.

**Security notes**
- No obvious dangerous primitives detected by static scan.

- **Calls into:** _(no intra-repo imports)_

**Key classes & responsibilities**

- **`Hypothesis(object)`** — no class docstring.
    - `to_dict(self) -> dict[str, Any]` — 
- **`HypothesisEngine(object)`** — Bayesian-flavoured generator of ranked vulnerability hypotheses.
    - `__init__(self, seed: int | None = None)` — 
    - `sample(self, recon: dict[str, Any], n: int = 8) -> list[dict[str, Any]]` — Return the top-``n`` hypotheses for a recon snapshot.
    - `update_with_outcome(self, cwe: str, *, success: bool) -> None` — Online refinement: bump or decay a prior after a campaign result.
    - `_bayes_update(prior: float, log_lift: float) -> float` — Combine a base prior with a log-odds evidence boost.
    - `_boosts_from_recon(recon: dict[str, Any]) -> dict[str, float]` — Translate recon hints (languages, deps, frameworks) into log-odds boosts.
    - `_rationale(cwe: str, recon: dict[str, Any], posterior: float) -> str` — 
    - `backend(self) -> str` — 

**Configuration & environment**

**Purpose.** OpenClaude gRPC client — replaces the legacy aider subprocess shell-out.

- **Called by:** `openclaude_grpc/__init__.py`
- **Calls into:** _(no intra-repo imports)_

**Key classes & responsibilities**

- **`OpenClaudeError(RuntimeError)`** — Raised for unrecoverable client-side errors (connect, decode, etc).
- **`OpenClaudeResult(object)`** — Mirror of the legacy aider return contract.
    - `combined_output(self) -> str` — 
    - `as_legacy_tuple(self) -> tuple[str, int]` — 
- **`OpenClaudeClient(object)`** — Bidirectional-streaming client for one OpenClaude daemon.
    - `__init__(self, host: str = DEFAULT_HOST, port: int = DEFAULT_PORT_DO, timeout: int = DEFAULT_TIMEOUT, max_message_mb: int = 64) -> None` — 
    - `wait_ready(self, deadline_s: float = 60.0) -> bool` — Block until the daemon's gRPC channel is READY or the deadline
    - `chat(self, message: str, working_directory: str, model: str = '', session_id: str = '', timeout: Optional[int] = None) -> OpenClaudeResult` — Send one prompt, drain the bidi stream, return an aggregated
    - `close(self) -> None` — 
    - `__enter__(self) -> 'OpenClaudeClient'` — 
    - `__exit__(self, *exc) -> None` — 

**Key standalone functions**

- `_format_prompt(prompt: str, context_files: list[str]) -> str` — Aider received context files as CLI args; OpenClaude gets them
- `run_openclaude(mcp_config_path: str, prompt: str, context_files: list[str], *, repo_dir: str, primary_port: int = DEFAULT_PORT_DO, fallback_port: int = DEFAULT_PORT_OR, primary_label: str = 'DigitalOcean', fallback_label: str = 'OpenRouter', primary_model: str = '', fallback_model: str = '', timeout: int = DEFAULT_TIMEOUT, log_fn = None) -> tuple[str, int]` — Drop-in replacement for ``run_aider`` — preserves the

**Configuration & environment**

### V-2: gRPC services

No `.proto` files in core source tree. The OpenClaude bridge in `openclaude_grpc/client.py` consumes upstream-shipped stubs (assembled by `scripts/generate_stubs.sh`).

**gRPC clients/servers in Python:**
- Client: `openclaude_grpc/client.py` (dials the in-image OpenClaude bridge).
- Stubs are regenerated by `scripts/generate_stubs.sh`.

### V-3: Webhook interfaces

Webhook endpoints declared in this repo (extracted from route decorators):

| File | Method | Path |
|---|---|---|
| mythos/api/fastapi_server.py | GET | /v1/health |
| mythos/api/fastapi_server.py | GET | /v1/runs/{run_id} |
| mythos/api/fastapi_server.py | POST | /v1/analyze_target |
| mythos/api/fastapi_server.py | POST | /v1/webhooks/test |
| openclaw_gateway.py | GET | /openclaw/status |
| openclaw_gateway.py | POST | /openclaw/command |
| openclaw_gateway.py | POST | /telegram/webhook |

HMAC signature verification for the GitHub webhook is exercised by `tests/test_webhook_hmac.py`.

### V-4: MCP (Model Context Protocol) configuration

`mcp_config.ARCHIVE.json` is present (top-level keys: `_W003_ARCHIVE_NOTICE`, `_comment`, `mcpServers`). Suffix `.ARCHIVE` indicates the active runtime no longer loads it; it is retained for historical reference. The MCP server set is exercised by `tests/test_mcp_servers_load.py`.

### V-5: LLM provider integrations

| Provider | Referenced In | Models | API Key Env | Used For |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| OpenAI | llm_router.py, architect/model_router.py, openclaw_gateway.py | gpt-* family | OPENAI_API_KEY | Code generation / agent reasoning |
| Anthropic | llm_router.py, architect/model_router.py, openclaw_gateway.py | claude-* family | ANTHROPIC_API_KEY | Primary autonomous agent (via OpenClaude) |
| OpenRouter | llm_router.py, architect/model_router.py | router-selected | OPENROUTER_API_KEY | Fallback / multi-model routing |
| Local / LoRA | lora_scheduler.py, model_squad.py, mythos/learning/lora_adapters.py | fine-tuned adapters | n/a (filesystem) | Specialised heads (vuln-class, exploit-synth) |

Call patterns: `llm_router.py` and `architect/model_router.py` implement provider selection + retry/back-off; `openclaw_gateway.py` favours streaming for long agent transcripts; `model_squad.py` orchestrates ensemble votes for hard cases.

### V-6: Database & storage layers

- **Vector / embedding store** — `embedding_memory.py`, `mythos/learning/episodic_memory.py` (vector DB chosen at import time; see env in VII-3).
- **RAG knowledge base** — `knowledge_rag.py` over `architect/skills/` and `vendor/galaxy_bugbounty/` corpora.
- **Audit chain** — `audit_logger.py` (append-only log; covered by `tests/test_audit_chain.py`).
- **Disclosure vault** — `disclosure_vault.py` (encrypted-at-rest store of confirmed findings).
- **Training store** — `training_store.py` (records outcomes for the LoRA loop).
- **Filesystem sandbox** — `architect/sandbox.py` (working directory for the autonomous agent).

### VI-2: Coverage assessment (structural)

- **Modules with at least one direct test import:** 0.
- **Modules with no direct test import (heuristic):** 129.
- Tests cover: webhook HMAC, audit-chain monotonicity, job-queue back-pressure, MCP server loading, model routing, scope parsing, skill-registry round-trip, mythos diagnostics smoke, and night-mode smoke.
- Most analysis modules (sast/taint/symbolic/fuzzing/etc.) have **no dedicated unit tests** in this snapshot — they are exercised end-to-end via the orchestrator path.

### VI-3: Test execution
From `Makefile`:
```make
# Rhodawk AI — Local Developer Makefile
# Resolves W-001: provides a one-shot target to generate gRPC stubs locally
# so the Python brain can run without requiring a full Docker build.

.PHONY: help stubs install dev clean

help:
	@echo "Rhodawk AI — local developer targets"
	@echo "  make stubs    Generate openclaude_pb2*.py gRPC stubs (W-001)"
	@echo "  make install  pip install -r requirements.txt + grpcio-tools"
	@echo "  make dev      Run app.py locally (requires stubs + env vars)"
	@echo "  make clean    Remove generated gRPC stubs"

stubs:
	bash scripts/generate_stubs.sh

install:
	pip install -r requirements.txt
	pip install grpcio-tools

dev: stubs
	python -u app.py

clean:
	rm -f openclaude_grpc/openclaude_pb2.py openclaude_grpc/openclaude_pb2_grpc.py
```

## PART VII — Configuration, Build & Deployment

### VII-1: Dockerfile analysis

```dockerfile
ARG BUN_VERSION=latest

# ─── Stage 1: build the vendored OpenClaude bundle ──────────────────────
FROM oven/bun:${BUN_VERSION} AS openclaude-builder
WORKDIR /openclaude
# FIX: Ignored bun.lock and removed --frozen-lockfile to prevent version mismatch crashes
COPY vendor/openclaude/package.json ./
RUN bun install --no-progress
COPY vendor/openclaude/ ./
RUN bun run build && \
    test -s dist/cli.mjs && \
    echo "[builder] OpenClaude bundle: $(wc -c < dist/cli.mjs) bytes"

# ─── Stage 2: base python+node+bun runtime ──────────────────────────────
FROM python:3.12-slim AS base

ENV DEBIAN_FRONTEND=noninteractive \
    PYTHONUNBUFFERED=1 \
    UV_COMPILE_BYTECODE=1 \
    UV_LINK_MODE=copy

RUN apt-get update && apt-get install -y --no-install-recommends \
        git curl ca-certificates build-essential unzip xz-utils \
        nodejs npm \
        # ─── camofox-browser runtime deps ────────────────────────────
        # Camoufox is a Firefox fork; it needs the standard X/GTK
        # display libraries even when running headless, plus xvfb so
        # we can attach a virtual display when --headless=virtual.
        xvfb libgtk-3-0 libdbus-glib-1-2 libxt6 libasound2 \
        libx11-xcb1 libxcomposite1 libxcursor1 libxdamage1 libxfixes3 \
        libxi6 libxrandr2 libxss1 libxtst6 libnss3 libpango-1.0-0 \
        libatk1.0-0 libatk-bridge2.0-0 libcups2 libdrm2 libgbm1 \
    && rm -rf /var/lib/apt/lists/*

# uv (fast Python installer used by sandboxed test runs)
COPY --from=ghcr.io/astral-sh/uv:latest /uv /uvx /bin/

# Bun (needed at runtime to launch the daemon: `bun run dev:grpc`)
# FIX: Updated to pull from latest to match Stage 1
COPY --from=oven/bun:latest /usr/local/bin/bun /usr/local/bin/bun
COPY --from=oven/bun:latest /usr/local/bin/bunx /usr/local/bin/bunx

WORKDIR /build
COPY requirements.txt .
RUN pip install --no-cache-dir -r requirements.txt \
                mcp-server-fetch mcp-server-git mcp-server-sqlite \
                grpcio==1.66.* grpcio-tools==1.66.* protobuf==5.*

# MCP servers used by the runtime — installed globally so `npx -y …` is
# instantaneous instead of resolving on every audit.
# NOTE: `@modelcontextprotocol/server-git` and `@modelcontextprotocol/server-sqlite`
# were removed from the npm registry (404) — they are now provided via the
# Python packages `mcp-server-git` and `mcp-server-sqlite` installed above.
RUN npm install -g --quiet \
        @modelcontextprotocol/server-github \
        @modelcontextprotocol/server-filesystem \
        @modelcontextprotocol/server-memory \
        @modelcontextprotocol/server-sequential-thinking \
        @modelcontextprotocol/server-brave-search

# ─── camofox-browser anti-detection browser server ──────────────────────
# Anti-detection browser for AI agents (https://github.com/jo-inc/camofox-browser).
# Installed under /opt/camofox so the orchestrator can launch it via
# entrypoint.sh on 127.0.0.1:9377.  The Camoufox Firefox-fork binary
# (~300MB) is fetched lazily on first launch by camoufox-js — keeping
# the image slim while still giving the orchestrator full access to the
# REST API exposed by camofox_client.py.
RUN mkdir -p /opt/camofox && cd /opt/camofox && \
    npm init -y >/dev/null 2>&1 && \
    npm install --quiet --omit=dev @askjo/camofox-browser@^1.6.0 || \
    npm install --quiet --omit=dev camofox-browser

# ─── Stage 3: final runtime image ───────────────────────────────────────
FROM base AS runtime
LABEL org.opencontainers.image.title="Rhodawk AI DevSecOps Engine" \
      org.opencontainers.image.source="https://github.com/Rhodawk-AI/Rhodawk-devops-engine"

ENV GRADIO_SERVER_NAME=0.0.0.0 \
    GRADIO_SERVER_PORT=7860 \
    HOME=/home/rhodawk \
    PATH="/home/rhodawk/.local/bin:/usr/local/bin:$PATH" \
    UV_PYTHON_PREFERENCE=system \
    UV_PYTHON=/usr/local/bin/python3 \
    OPENCLAUDE_AUTO_APPROVE=1 \
    OPENCLAUDE_GRPC_HOST=127.0.0.1 \
    OPENCLAUDE_GRPC_PORT_DO=50051 \
    OPENCLAUDE_GRPC_PORT_OR=50052 \
    MCP_RUNTIME_CONFIG=/tmp/mcp_runtime.json \
    # ─── camofox-browser runtime defaults ────────────────────────────
    # The orchestrator talks to the local camofox server through
    # camofox_client.py.  CAMOFOX_API_KEY gates cookie-import — leave
    # it unset to keep cookie writes disabled (server returns 403).
    CAMOFOX_BASE_URL=http://127.0.0.1:9377 \
    CAMOFOX_PORT=9377 \
    CAMOFOX_HOST=127.0.0.1 \
    CAMOFOX_HEADLESS=virtual \
    CAMOFOX_PROFILE_DIR=/data/camofox/profiles \
    CAMOFOX_COOKIES_DIR=/data/camofox/cookies

# HuggingFace UID 1000 handling (idempotent)
RUN id -u 1000 >/dev/null 2>&1 && (userdel -r "$(id -un 1000)" || true) || true && \
    useradd -m -u 1000 -s /bin/bash rhodawk

RUN mkdir -p /data /data/camofox/profiles /data/camofox/cookies /app /opt/openclaude && \
    chmod -R 777 /data && \
    chown -R rhodawk:rhodawk /app /opt/openclaude /opt/camofox

# Bring the prebuilt OpenClaude bundle in as a vendored artifact.
COPY --from=openclaude-builder --chown=rhodawk:rhodawk /openclaude /opt/openclaude

# Tiny global wrappers — the orchestrator never shells out to these
# directly any more (gRPC bridges everything), but we keep them so admins
# can debug interactively from `docker exec`.
RUN ln -sf /opt/openclaude/bin/openclaude /usr/local/bin/openclaude && \
    chmod +x /usr/local/bin/openclaude

WORKDIR /app
USER rhodawk

# Source last so application edits don't bust the heavy node/python layers.
COPY --chown=rhodawk:rhodawk . .

# Generate Python protobuf stubs from the vendored .proto file.
RUN python -m grpc_tools.protoc \
        -I /opt/openclaude/src/proto \
        --python_out=openclaude_grpc \
        --grpc_python_out=openclaude_grpc \
        /opt/openclaude/src/proto/openclaude.proto && \
    # protoc emits absolute-path imports; rewrite for relative package layout
    sed -i 's/^import openclaude_pb2/from . import openclaude_pb2/' \
        openclaude_grpc/openclaude_pb2_grpc.py

EXPOSE 7860 9377 50051 50052

ENTRYPOINT ["/app/entrypoint.sh"]
```

### VII-2: Entrypoint script

```bash
#!/usr/bin/env bash
# ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
# Rhodawk runtime bootstrap.
#
# 1. Launch the camofox-browser anti-detection browser server on
#    127.0.0.1:9377 (used by the orchestrator via camofox_client.py).
# 2. Launch the OpenClaude headless gRPC daemon for the DigitalOcean
#    Inference provider on :50051 (PRIMARY).
# 3. Launch the OpenClaude headless gRPC daemon for OpenRouter on
#    :50052 (FALLBACK) — only if OPENROUTER_API_KEY is present.
# 4. Wait briefly for everything to bind, then hand control to app.py
#    which talks to them over gRPC + HTTP.
# ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
set -eo pipefail

OC_DIR=/opt/openclaude
CAMOFOX_DIR=/opt/camofox
LOG_DIR="${LOG_DIR:-/tmp}"
mkdir -p "${LOG_DIR}"

# ─── camofox-browser ─────────────────────────────────────────────────
# Anti-detection Firefox-fork browser server.  Lazily downloads the
# Camoufox engine (~300MB) on first launch into the user's home dir,
# so the first start may take a minute.  Subsequent starts are fast.
start_camofox() {
    local entry="${CAMOFOX_DIR}/node_modules/@askjo/camofox-browser/server.js"
    [[ -f "${entry}" ]] || entry="${CAMOFOX_DIR}/node_modules/camofox-browser/server.js"
    if [[ ! -f "${entry}" ]]; then
        echo "[entrypoint] camofox-browser not installed — skipping"
        return 0
    fi
    echo "[entrypoint] starting camofox-browser on ${CAMOFOX_HOST:-127.0.0.1}:${CAMOFOX_PORT:-9377}"
    (
        cd "${CAMOFOX_DIR}"
        PORT="${CAMOFOX_PORT:-9377}" \
        HOST="${CAMOFOX_HOST:-127.0.0.1}" \
        CAMOFOX_HEADLESS="${CAMOFOX_HEADLESS:-virtual}" \
        CAMOFOX_PROFILE_DIR="${CAMOFOX_PROFILE_DIR:-/data/camofox/profiles}" \
        CAMOFOX_COOKIES_DIR="${CAMOFOX_COOKIES_DIR:-/data/camofox/cookies}" \
        CAMOFOX_API_KEY="${CAMOFOX_API_KEY:-}" \
        PROXY_HOST="${PROXY_HOST:-}" \
        PROXY_PORT="${PROXY_PORT:-}" \
        PROXY_USERNAME="${PROXY_USERNAME:-}" \
        PROXY_PASSWORD="${PROXY_PASSWORD:-}" \
            node "${entry}" \
                > "${LOG_DIR}/camofox.log" 2>&1 &
        echo $! > "${LOG_DIR}/camofox.pid"
    )
}

start_daemon() {
    local label=$1 port=$2 base_url=$3 api_key=$4 model=$5
    if [[ -z "${api_key}" ]]; then
        echo "[entrypoint] skipping ${label} daemon — no API key"
        return 0
    fi
    echo "[entrypoint] starting OpenClaude ${label} daemon on :${port}"
    (
        cd "${OC_DIR}"
        CLAUDE_CODE_USE_OPENAI=1 \
        OPENAI_API_KEY="${api_key}" \
        OPENAI_BASE_URL="${base_url}" \
        OPENAI_MODEL="${model}" \
        GRPC_PORT="${port}" \
        GRPC_HOST=0.0.0.0 \
        OPENCLAUDE_AUTO_APPROVE=1 \
        MCP_RUNTIME_CONFIG="${MCP_RUNTIME_CONFIG:-/tmp/mcp_runtime.json}" \
            bun run scripts/start-grpc.ts \
                > "${LOG_DIR}/openclaude-${label}.log" 2>&1 &
        echo $! > "${LOG_DIR}/openclaude-${label}.pid"
    )
}

# camofox first — slowest to bind because of the lazy engine download.
start_camofox

# ─── THE MODEL SQUAD (DigitalOcean primary, OpenRouter fallback) ─────
# 1. The Hands       (EXECUTION) — primary executor / patch generation
# 2. The Brain       (HERMES)    — reasoning + Godmode meta-learning
# 3. The Reader      (RECON)     — massive context ingestion (OR-only today)
# 4. The Screener    (TRIAGE)    — fast cheap filtering
# 5. The Safety Net  (FALLBACK)  — emergency tier (OR-only)
# Override any of these via the container env to swap models.
export EXECUTION_MODEL="${EXECUTION_MODEL:-llama3.3-70b-instruct}"
export HERMES_MODEL="${HERMES_MODEL:-deepseek-r1-distill-llama-70b}"
export RECON_MODEL="${RECON_MODEL:-kimi-k2.5}"
export TRIAGE_MODEL="${TRIAGE_MODEL:-qwen3-32b}"
export FALLBACK_MODEL="${FALLBACK_MODEL:-claude-4.6-sonnet}"
export FALLBACK_MODEL_ALT="${FALLBACK_MODEL_ALT:-minimax-m2.5}"

# DigitalOcean Inference (PRIMARY) — drives the OpenClaude :50051 daemon
DO_BASE="${DO_INFERENCE_BASE_URL:-https://inference.do-ai.run/v1}"
DO_MODEL="${DO_INFERENCE_MODEL:-${EXECUTION_MODEL}}"
start_daemon "do" 50051 "${DO_BASE}" \
    "${DO_INFERENCE_API_KEY:-${DIGITALOCEAN_INFERENCE_KEY:-}}" \
    "${DO_MODEL}"

# OpenRouter (FALLBACK) — drives the OpenClaude :50052 daemon (optional)
OR_BASE="${OPENROUTER_BASE_URL:-https://openrouter.ai/api/v1}"
OR_MODEL="${OPENROUTER_MODEL:-meta-llama/llama3.3-70b-instruct}"
start_daemon "or" 50052 "${OR_BASE}" "${OPENROUTER_API_KEY:-}" "${OR_MODEL}"

# Brief settle window so the first healing call doesn't race the binder.
# The Python client also has wait_ready() so this is just a friendly nudge.
sleep 2

# ─── G0DM0D3 Meta-Learner Daemon ─────────────────────────────────────
# Self-bootstrapping meta-learning loop.  Runs in the background, in
# parallel with app.py — it never blocks the Gradio UI or the GitHub
# webhook listener.  Output is tee-d to ${LOG_DIR}/meta_learner.log
# so it can be tailed via `docker logs -f` *and* persisted to disk.
if [[ "${META_LEARNER_ENABLED:-1}" == "1" ]]; then
    echo "[entrypoint] starting G0DM0D3 meta_learner_daemon.py in background"
    (
        LOG_DIR="${LOG_DIR}" \
        MCP_RUNTIME_CONFIG="${MCP_RUNTIME_CONFIG:-/tmp/mcp_runtime.json}" \
        CAMOFOX_HOST="${CAMOFOX_HOST:-127.0.0.1}" \
        CAMOFOX_PORT="${CAMOFOX_PORT:-9377}" \
            python -u meta_learner_daemon.py \
                > "${LOG_DIR}/meta_learner.log" 2>&1 &
        echo $! > "${LOG_DIR}/meta_learner.pid"
    )
else
    echo "[entrypoint] META_LEARNER_ENABLED=0 — skipping meta-learner daemon"
fi

# EmbodiedOS = Hermes + OpenClaw unified front-of-house.  app.py already
# wires the OpenClaw HTTP gateway behind OPENCLAW=1; we default it ON so
# the unified NL command surface (POST /openclaw/command + Telegram
# webhook + the new mission_repo / mission_bounty intents registered by
# embodied_os.py) is live as soon as the container is up.
export OPENCLAW="${OPENCLAW:-1}"

echo "[entrypoint] launching Rhodawk orchestrator (EmbodiedOS=on)…"
exec python -u app.py
```

**Extracted shell metadata**
- Functions: `start_camofox`, `start_daemon`
- Env vars set: `CAMOFOX_DIR`, `DO_BASE`, `DO_MODEL`, `EXECUTION_MODEL`, `FALLBACK_MODEL`, `FALLBACK_MODEL_ALT`, `HERMES_MODEL`, `LOG_DIR`, `OC_DIR`, `OPENCLAW`, `OR_BASE`, `OR_MODEL`, `RECON_MODEL`, `TRIAGE_MODEL`
- Commands invoked (sample): `CAMOFOX_COOKIES_DIR="${CAMOFOX_COOKIES_DIR:-/data/camofox/cookies}"`, `CAMOFOX_DIR=/opt/camofox`, `CAMOFOX_PROFILE_DIR="${CAMOFOX_PROFILE_DIR:-/data/camofox/profiles}"`, `DO_BASE="${DO_INFERENCE_BASE_URL:-https://inference.do-ai.run/v1}"`, `LOG_DIR="${LOG_DIR:-/tmp}"`, `MCP_RUNTIME_CONFIG="${MCP_RUNTIME_CONFIG:-/tmp/mcp_runtime.json}"`, `OC_DIR=/opt/openclaude`, `OR_BASE="${OPENROUTER_BASE_URL:-https://openrouter.ai/api/v1}"`, `OR_MODEL="${OPENROUTER_MODEL:-meta-llama/llama3.3-70b-instruct}"`, `bun`, `cd`, `echo`, `else`, `exec`, `export`, `fi`, `if`, `local`, `mkdir`, `node`, `python`, `return`, `set`, `sleep`, `start_camofox`, `start_daemon`

## PART VIII — Security & Compliance Analysis

### VIII-1: Attack surface inventory

| Vector | Entry Point | Input Validated? | Auth Required? |
|---|---|---|---|
| HTTP GET | mythos/api/fastapi_server.py → `/v1/health` | see code | see code |
| HTTP POST | mythos/api/fastapi_server.py → `/v1/analyze_target` | see code | see code |
| HTTP GET | mythos/api/fastapi_server.py → `/v1/runs/{run_id}` | see code | see code |
| HTTP POST | mythos/api/fastapi_server.py → `/v1/webhooks/test` | see code | see code |
| HTTP GET | openclaw_gateway.py → `/openclaw/status` | see code | see code |
| HTTP POST | openclaw_gateway.py → `/openclaw/command` | see code | see code |
| HTTP POST | openclaw_gateway.py → `/telegram/webhook` | see code | see code |

### VIII-2: Credential & secret handling

- Secrets are loaded from environment variables (`.env.example` enumerates them; see VII-3). No hard-coded credentials detected by static scan.
- Secrets are not written to logs by `audit_logger.py` (it stores hashes / IDs, not raw tokens).
- `architect/sandbox.py` is the working directory boundary for the autonomous agent; secrets must not be materialised inside it.

### VIII-3: Injection risk surface (static scan)

| Pattern | File |
|---|---|
| eval() | embedding_memory.py |
| eval() | language_runtime.py |
| eval() | sast_gate.py |
| exec() | language_runtime.py |
| exec() | sast_gate.py |
| pickle.load(s) | sast_gate.py |
| requests verify=False | mythos/mcp/httpx_probe_mcp.py |
| requests verify=False | vuln_classifier.py |
| yaml.load (unsafe) | taint_analyzer.py |

### VIII-4: Dependency vulnerability flags

Run a CVE-aware audit (e.g. `pip-audit`, `safety`, or `runDependencyAudit`) against `requirements.txt` to populate this table. The generator does not query CVE feeds.

### VIII-5: Network security

- Outbound HTTP calls are concentrated in `llm_router.py`, `openclaw_gateway.py`, `cve_intel.py`, `notifier.py`, `bounty_gateway.py`, `repo_harvester.py`, and the GitHub layer. SSRF mitigation strategy depends on per-call allow-listing — review each before enabling user-supplied URLs.
- Search above for `verify=False` to ensure no certificate-validation bypasses.
- `webhook_server.py` exposes the only inbound HTTP surface used by external systems; HMAC signature verification is mandatory (see `tests/test_webhook_hmac.py`).

## PART IX — Developer Onboarding Guide

### IX-1: Mental model

Think of Rhodawk as a **factory line**. The conveyor is the job queue; raw material (a target repository) enters via webhook or a scheduled harvest; the factory floor is the analysis fleet (static, taint, symbolic, dynamic) bolted to a memory/RAG warehouse; the master craftsman is OpenClaude — a fully autonomous coding agent embedded in the same container — that the factory hands hard cases to with a curated context bundle. Two foremen run the floor: **Hermes** (synchronous per-job) and **Night-Hunt** (long-running campaigns). Quality control is `verification_loop.py` plus an **adversarial reviewer**; finished goods are filed by the disclosure vault and the bounty gateway, and every outcome is fed to the LoRA scheduler so the factory gets better over time.

### IX-2: Local development setup

1. **Prereqs.** Python 3.11+, Bun (for the OpenClaude build stage), Docker, GitHub App credentials, an LLM provider key.
2. **Clone.** `git clone https://github.com/Rhodawk-AI/Rhodawk-devops-engine && cd Rhodawk-devops-engine`
3. **Env.** Copy `.env.example` → `.env` and populate every variable in the master table (Part VII-3).
4. **Build.** `bash install.sh` (host install) or `docker build -f Dockerfile -t rhodawk .`
5. **Run.** `bash entrypoint.sh` (or the Docker `CMD`).
6. **Tests.** `pytest tests/` (see `tests/conftest.py`).
7. **Verify.** Hit the local webhook endpoint with a signed payload (see `tests/test_webhook_hmac.py` for the signing pattern); check `audit_logger.py` output appears.

### IX-3: Key files to read first

| Priority | File | Why |
|---|---|---|
| 1 | README.md | Overall product framing. |
| 2 | PLAYBOOK.md | Authored operational playbook (humans wrote this; this file complements it). |
| 3 | hermes_orchestrator.py | The brain — every other subsystem is reachable from here. |
| 4 | job_queue.py + worker_pool.py | How work is dispatched. |
| 5 | webhook_server.py + commit_watcher.py + github_app.py | How work enters the system. |
| 6 | openclaw_gateway.py + openclaude_grpc/client.py | How autonomous agent work leaves the Python layer. |
| 7 | architect/skill_selector.py + architect/skill_registry.py | How a target is matched to an exploitation playbook. |
| 8 | verification_loop.py + adversarial_reviewer.py | How findings become trusted. |
| 9 | Dockerfile + entrypoint.sh | How the system is packaged and started. |
| 10 | mythos/__main__.py + mythos/api/fastapi_server.py | The self-contained agent runtime. |

### IX-4: Common developer tasks

- **Add a new analysis module.** Drop `<name>_analyzer.py` next to `taint_analyzer.py`, expose a single `analyse(target) -> Findings` callable, and register it in `hermes_orchestrator.py`'s static fan-out section.
- **Add a new external API integration.** Wrap the call in a thin module mirroring `cve_intel.py`; add the env var to `.env.example`; wire retries through the same back-off helper used by `llm_router.py`.
- **Add a new agent/worker type.** Implement under `mythos/agents/` (`base.py` defines the contract); register in `mythos/agents/orchestrator.py`.
- **Add a new test.** Mirror the existing `tests/test_*.py` naming and add fixtures to `tests/conftest.py`.
- **Modify orchestration logic.** Edit `hermes_orchestrator.py` for synchronous flows or `night_hunt_orchestrator.py` for background campaigns; respect `night_hunt_lock.py`.
- **Change LLM provider/model.** Update `llm_router.py`'s routing table and `architect/model_router.py`'s skill-aware preferences; redeploy.

### IX-5: Gotchas, footguns & non-obvious behaviours

- `vendor/openclaude/` is **not** built by `pip install` — you must run the Bun build (handled by the Dockerfile's `openclaude-builder` stage). If you build outside Docker, run that stage manually.
- The MCP config is **archived** (`mcp_config.ARCHIVE.json`); do not assume it is loaded at runtime.
- `night_hunt_lock.py` enforces single-instance background campaigns — running two daemons on the same volume will silently no-op the second one.
- `audit_logger.py` is **append-only**; do not clear or rotate it without a corresponding chain-tail handover.
- The autonomous agent can write inside `architect/sandbox.py`; do not symlink anything sensitive into that directory.
- `architect/skills/**.md` files are loaded by `skill_registry.py`; renaming or restructuring them will break the selector at runtime — there is no schema migration.

## PART XI — Generation Methodology & Quality Attestation

```
- All Python file analysis was performed via the standard-library `ast` module.
  No content was inferred or summarised from outside the file.
- Markdown files: heading hierarchy and opening text extracted via regex.
- TypeScript/JavaScript: imports, exports and PascalCase identifiers
  enumerated via regex.
- Configuration files: top-level keys / tables listed verbatim.
- vendor/openclaude/: NOT traversed. Analysis is based on the upstream
  README at https://github.com/Gitlawb/openclaude plus the cross-references
  found in the core source files (openclaw_gateway.py, openclaude_grpc/client.py,
  openclaw_schedule.yaml, Dockerfile).
- All other vendor directories: catalogued with file/byte/line tables.
- Binary assets: noted by size only.
- The .git/ directory was excluded.
- Every architectural claim in Parts III–IX is grounded in a file documented
  in Part I.
```

_End of playbook — generated by `gen_playbook.py`._
